  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_38f9e26e-3a83-4ed1-8a57-8125542902dc'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer12619168913195219436">Nina Sheridan desperately needs a timeout vacation. With a fiancé who can't even remember how she takes her coffee, Nina wants some distance to rethink her engagement. Flying halfway around the world from England to a mountain town in Colorado should do the trick. But when she finds a gorgeous man at her rental cabin, Nina's cold, lonely adventure suddenly heats up.<br/><br/>The own</span>
  <span id="freeText12619168913195219436" style="display:none">Nina Sheridan desperately needs a timeout vacation. With a fiancé who can't even remember how she takes her coffee, Nina wants some distance to rethink her engagement. Flying halfway around the world from England to a mountain town in Colorado should do the trick. But when she finds a gorgeous man at her rental cabin, Nina's cold, lonely adventure suddenly heats up.<br /><br />The owner of the house, Holden "Max" Maxwell is surprised by the beautiful woman who turns up at his door. But when Nina becomes ill, Max spends days nursing her back to health. A private man with a broken heart, Max finds himself drawn to the strong-willed woman. Soon it becomes impossible for Nina and Max to deny their growing attraction to one another. Yet even as these two wounded lovebirds think about taking a chance on a relationship, a dangerous secret from Max's past emerges-and threatens to end their love for good.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10361418215763204146"><b>4.5 Wonder Max Stars</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/fan_zpsxizprgnd.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462366072ra/18987916.gif' alt=' photo fan_zpsxizprgnd.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>“Duchess?” He threw his other hand out, his gaze drifting the length of me as he said, “Fancy-ass clothes, fancy-ass purse, fancy-ass boots, fancy-ass accent.” His eyes came to my face and he finished firmly. “Duchess.”-Nina and Max</b><br/><br/><b> Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Ok so this is only the 4th book by Kristen Ashley that I have read. The other 3 being the books from the Three Series which is her PNR series. The Three Series was iffy for me. I hated the first book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13453301.Until_the_Sun_Falls_from_the_Sky__The_Three___1_' title='Until the Sun Falls from the Sky (The Three, #1) by Kristen Ashley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Until the Sun Falls from the Sky</a> wi</span>
  <span id="freeText10361418215763204146" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Wonder Max Stars</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/fan_zpsxizprgnd.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462366072ra/18987916.gif" alt=" photo fan_zpsxizprgnd.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>“Duchess?” He threw his other hand out, his gaze drifting the length of me as he said, “Fancy-ass clothes, fancy-ass purse, fancy-ass boots, fancy-ass accent.” His eyes came to my face and he finished firmly. “Duchess.”-Nina and Max</b><br><br><b> Spoilers</b><br><br>Ok so this is only the 4th book by Kristen Ashley that I have read. The other 3 being the books from the Three Series which is her PNR series. The Three Series was iffy for me. I hated the first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13453301.Until_the_Sun_Falls_from_the_Sky__The_Three___1_" title="Until the Sun Falls from the Sky (The Three, #1) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Until the Sun Falls from the Sky</a> with a deep passion. I hated that hero so much I thought my head was gonna pop off. Then I loved the second book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15817326.With_Everything_I_Am__The_Three___2_" title="With Everything I Am (The Three, #2) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">With Everything I Am</a> and the third book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17346804.Wild_and_Free__The_Three___3_" title="Wild and Free (The Three, #3) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Wild and Free</a> was just Meh for me. So I have been putting off reading any more Kristen Ashley books afraid of what I would get. But because a ton of my friends love KA and brag about how great her books are I thought I would give her another shot. I'm so glad I did. I loved this book, but boy is it a big book. 629 pages but never was I bored. Also because the book was so big it never felt rushed. There was great character, and relationship development in this book that I felt like I really got their whole story. <br><br><b>“Jesus,” he muttered, dropping his head. “What?” He looked back at me. “Duchess, you can argue about anything.” “No I can’t.” “So, now you’re arguin’ about not arguing?”-Max and Nina</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/jgghyfgdyhg_zpsanhoqgkk.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462366072i/18987917._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo jgghyfgdyhg_zpsanhoqgkk.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>“Has anyone told you you’re domineering?” “Nope.” “Well, let me be the first. You’re domineering.”-Nina and Max</b><br><br>Max was amazing for me. AMAZING!!!! I fucking loved him. He was super sexy, totally domineering, and could be really sweet. Max for me was the perfect Alpha male. He had all the yummy qualities of a bossy, protective , possessive Alpha without going over that line into abusive controlling dickwad. I loved that even though Max is a widow and even though he really loved his dead wife, I never felt like Nina came second. I never felt like he compared the two, never felt like she had to compete with a ghost. Hell he never even brought Anna(Dead wife) up until almost the end and that was after he found out she already knew almost the whole time they had been together. Max didn't come off bitter, mean or uncaring. In fact he treated Nina great was thoughtful, romantic, and supportive. Truly Max made this book for me. <br><br><b>"Shut up and kiss me, Duchess." "Max!" "All right, I'll kiss you.” -Max and Nina</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/julie-andrews-gif-julie-andrews-practically-perfect-in-every-way-mp_zpsjmcpvidk.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462366072ra/18987918.gif" alt=" photo julie-andrews-gif-julie-andrews-practically-perfect-in-every-way-mp_zpsjmcpvidk.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>“Fucked her last night, man, and this morning. Five times. Five. It was like she hadn’t been touched in a decade. So fuckin’ sweet. Damn,” he taunted, his eyes locked on Niles. “You’ve had her, you gotta know, not enough money in the world’s worth that.” -Max</b><br><br>Nina I also really liked, not as much as Max but damn close. Nina wasn't perfect, but her flaws made her endearing for the most part. The only thing she did that kinda annoyed me was all through the book she kept saying Sorry?...... Uhh....... HMMM..... I'm sorry.....mmmhmm...... Max....... I bet she said sorry at least 200 times in this book! Oh and I didn't really care for the fact that she had some major insecurities. It didn't make me dislike her but I wish she would have just talked to Max about her fears instead of getting all up in her head. Max may have never seen her as second to his dead wife or treated her that way but Nina seen herself that way. She just decided that because he loved Anna and she died that she was his one great love and she would never have his love. And that she would be his second and have to settle for being runner up if she stayed with me. And although I think any woman would have her doubts She should have talked to him about it like a grown up. He asked her a number of times what was wrong and each time she lied to him. That being said I still really liked her crazy, sassy, and funny self. The thing I loved the most about her was that she didn't take shit. If someone got in her face she would go off. I love that she stuck up for herself and the ones she loved like a little bulldog!<br><br><b>“Babe,” he replied, grinning then said no more. Still being helpful, I explained, “I know you think that word speaks volumes but, I have to tell you, it actually doesn’t.”-Max and Nina</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/4562829_zpsc1ut6ezg.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462366072ra/18987919.gif" alt=" photo 4562829_zpsc1ut6ezg.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>“Learned some things in my life, Duchess, one of the most important, you find a good woman, you take care of her.” “Please” “This happens between us, Duchess, I’d take care of you.” “Don’t” “Die doin’ it,” he vowed.” -Max and Nina</b><br><br>Nina and Max's relationship was cute. They bickered all the time. Neither one had a problem with speaking their mind or taking the other to task if they did something hurtful. There was some steamy sex in this book, but not so much that it was ott. I also liked that that sex happened towards the middle of the book. Giving them time to get to know each other. I loved Nina's mom and step dad. I also loved Mindy and was glad that she got her Hea in this book. Something I noticed right from the start was this book made me laugh. I laughed so much reading this book that my face hurt at times. I love that when a book can make me smile and laugh and just give me hours of happiness. I adored the HEA totally swoon worthy. I can't wait to try another KA book. <br><br><b>"I lucked out, baby," Max went on. "When I was young life handed me somethin' beautiful. Then it took it away. Ten years down the road, somethin' different, but no less beautiful, showed up right at my front door. I knew it almost the minute I saw it and nothin' has happened since to shake that. You think, findin' that in you, I'm gonna let you change my password, write me some fucked up note and walk away?"-Max </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10361418215763204146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_259681034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/259681034" />
    <a title="Misty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5048924-misty"><img alt="Misty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360473918p2/5048924.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/259681034?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misty" href="/user/show/5048924-misty">Misty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer259681034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12501444846553779204">I made it to page 1354 of 1466 before I decided to stop torturing myself (Kindle pages! The book isn't THAT long...though it sure felt like it).<br/><br/>The main character, Nina, is British (American really, but has a British Accent). I didn't like her. It's not that I disliked her, I just didn't like her. I found her very one dimensional, without depth to her character. And she says Um a lot. A LOT. I tried to use the find button to find a specific paragraph that really irked me, but I gave up after the</span>
  <span id="freeText12501444846553779204" style="display:none">I made it to page 1354 of 1466 before I decided to stop torturing myself (Kindle pages! The book isn't THAT long...though it sure felt like it).<br /><br />The main character, Nina, is British (American really, but has a British Accent). I didn't like her. It's not that I disliked her, I just didn't like her. I found her very one dimensional, without depth to her character. And she says Um a lot. A LOT. I tried to use the find button to find a specific paragraph that really irked me, but I gave up after the first 100 "Um.."'s. Here's how it went.<br /><br />Max "So you knew?"<br />Nina "Um..."<br />Max But you didn't tell me?"<br />Nina "Um..."<br />Max " How could you not have told me ?"<br />Nina "Um..."<br />Max " Didn't you know how that would hurt me? Jesus Nina!"<br />Nina "Um..."<br /><br />Ok, possibly not quite that bad, but seriously, there were quite a few "Jesus, shoot my head off now!" moments for me. If Nina wasn't bad enough, the rest of the characters were. Maybe it's because I'm from the west coast, and never been to Colorado,but none of them seemed real to me. Especially the way they talked. They were all over the top, and they were ALL eccentric. I can understand having a kookie mother, or neighbour, or main character, or sister... but when they're all competing it hurts my eyes!<br /><br />Max... I had to re-read his sentences SEVERAL times because they left critical words out. Not a grammatical error, either- as it was done throughout the book. I don't know why, perhaps people in Colorado talk like this, but I sincerely doubt it. It aggravated me to no end. Oh, and Max also says "Yeah" a lot, which bothered me. It seems British or Australian. "Nina, just don't do it again. Yeah?" But the main thing for me is that they ALL sounded alike, and none of them had any distinguishing characteristics. They were too cliche. Macho mountain man always protecting his woman, eccentric mother who wants to move in next door, crazy hermit neighbour...you get the idea.<br /><br />And Max...I have nothing against domineering men. I LOVED Fifty Shades, and I think that's why this was on my recommended list. But Max isn't the same. Sure he talks dirty, but it didn't turn me on. I didn't feel the chemistry between him or Nina either- I mean, he falls in love with her because she gets pissed at his cabin? Really? After that it was over, and he'd die for her. Oh, taking her car keys away? That kind of did it for me. She wasn't even angry (well,the book says she was angry, but I didn't see it!). The moment his lips touched hers, she was happy. I would love to meet a man whose lips are so magical, no matter how angry I was, I forgave him instantly and jumped on my back. Ugh.<br /><br />Take this review with a grain of salt, because I'm obviously a dissenter here. A book with this many 5 star reviews must have something going for it... I'm just not sure what. Maybe the sex scenes? They were pretty hot. But I can't even bring myself to finish the last 100 pages to find out who did it (the murder, which apparently is the "plot" of this book). I don't care- about who did it, or why, or even that the guy is dead. I grew up reading Harlequin romance novels, and while my literary palette has slowly graduated, I do still love to read beach novels and easy reads. I was hoping this would be one of them.<br /><br />Alas, all I can think is ick- and I'm glad I don't live in Colorado!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12501444846553779204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_247619577" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247619577" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247619577?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=book-1-of-my-fav-series">book-1-of-my-fav-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247619577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8401212965840211564"><b> <i> “In my life, I’ve learned when to let shit go and when to fight for it. This, babe, what we got, I’ll fight for.” </i></b> <br/><br/>What is it about Kristen Ashley’s books that just leaves you with the <i> warmest, fuzziest feelings </i> ever ? <br/><br/>They just reach right into your heart and connect you so deeply with each of the characters *big smile*. Absolutely LOVE her writing!! and I’m officially in love with Macho Mountain Max!!<br/><br/>Tired of her boring life with her bland and clueless fiance, Nina decides she needs a time</span>
  <span id="freeText8401212965840211564" style="display:none"><b> <i> “In my life, I’ve learned when to let shit go and when to fight for it. This, babe, what we got, I’ll fight for.” </i></b> <br><br>What is it about Kristen Ashley’s books that just leaves you with the <i> warmest, fuzziest feelings </i> ever ? <br><br>They just reach right into your heart and connect you so deeply with each of the characters *big smile*. Absolutely LOVE her writing!! and I’m officially in love with Macho Mountain Max!!<br><br>Tired of her boring life with her bland and clueless fiance, Nina decides she needs a timeout to rethink what she wants out of life and so she books an idealic 2-week stay in a gorgeous mountain house in Colorado. But things don’t quite go according to plan. She arrives in the middle of a bad storm, late, exhausted, coming down with a bad cold, only to find that there was a mix-up with the house and that the owner, swoony-gorgeous-Alpha-hot-Macho-mountain-man Max, is occupying it. At first, he wants nothing to do with her and tried to send her back to town to stay at a hotel. Frustrated by this huge wrench in her plans, Nina leaves in a huff only to end up in a ditch on the side of the road. Utterly depressed over her ruined timeout vacation plans, she bursts into tears and promptly falls asleep. When she wakes up some time later, she’s in a warm, fluffy bed back at Max’s house, and is changed, cleaned up and sick as a dog. And over the next several days, Max continues to look after her and nurse her back to health.<br><br>Right from the start, they have grin-enducing banter and Max just swoonily slips into her life. And, unphased by her many ruffled feathers, he starts convincing her to stay a while longer.. and take a gamble on him.<br><br><i> “You’re half a world away, Duchess, you been sick as a dog and your man doesn’t contact you?”…<br>“Niles is reserved,” I whispered.<br>“Niles is an ass,” He returned…<br>“You don’t know him.”…<br>“I’ve seen you naked, I’ve seen you sweet, I’ve seen you unsure and I’ve seen you riled and, seein’ all that ,I know, you were half a world away from me, I’d fuckin’ phone.” </i><br><br>Then, to add a little spice to the story, a local man is murdered, and, as with many KA books, there is a healthy dose of kidnappings, death threats, swoony seductions, second chances, brawls, shebitchesfromhell, healing, rape (happened to one of the side characters prior to the story), beautiful family moments, squee-worthy showdowns, plot twists…. oh, and did I mention the Macho Mountain Man?! <br><br>Oh, Max! Holden Maxwell. LOVED him! I loved how affectionate he was – both physically and verbally. He was always doing something sweet, calling her affectionate names, looking out for her, paying attention to the small stuff. I love that he just never let their relationship slide into the “stupid zone.” He was laid back, but at the same time deeply possessive and totally Alpha.<br><br><i> <b> “Found somethin’ I want, don’t tend to fuck around when that happens, Duchess. Ever.” </b> </i><br><br>Its kinda hard not to love a man who calls his woman ‘babe’, ‘darlin’ , ‘honey, baby and Duchess… and all in a sexy-as-all-hell gravelly voice… *swoooooon*<br><br><b> <i> “Learned some things in my life, Duchess, one of the most important, you find a good woman, you take care of her.”<br>“Please.”<br>“This happens between us, I’d take care you you.”<br>“Don’t.”<br>“Die doin’ it,” he vowed.“ </i></b> <br><br>Nina was also a surprisingly fun heroine. Sure, she fought his affections a little at first, but only to the extent that it was cute, not annoying. She could be soft and sweet at times, but had a totally tough-as-nails side and would take no shit from anyone or let anyone walk all over her or her friends. She was loyal, and I loved how she just ‘got’ some things – there were some characters with some serious hurt and trauma in this book, and she just totally knew how to handle it.<br><br>There’s a whole slew of side characters that we meet who become integral parts of the story. There is something just so deep about many of KA’s characters – little gestures and actions that convey a world of understanding or tell you so much about a character. I just love it! It connects you so strongly to the story.<br><br>The pacing of the book just never lets up – you go from funny to swoony to action-packed to oh-my-god to *squeeeee* to fanning yourself to heart in your throat – its just non-stop and keeps you flipping the pages!<br><br>It had me smiling right from the beginning! KA’s writing style is so effortless and easy to connect to – I could literally just see the story enfold in front of me as though I were watching a movie. My first sitting reading this book, it kept me riveted to the story until 5am!<br><br>This book was not quite as light-hearted as the Rock Chick series and not quite as badass as the Dream Man series. It was just about a real life, super-swoony Alpha guy finding his woman and I loved every minute of it. It’s the perfect kind of story you can just loose yourself in <br><br><i> “I’m not making out with you in a bar.”<br>“Why not?”<br>“Why?”<br>His face dipped closer. “Because, first, I want you to. And second… guys are checkin’ you out and that’d be me stakin’ my claim.”<br>“Staking your claim?”<br>“Its a guy thing.”<br>“Its a Macho Mountain Man thing.”<br>“Same thing.”<br>“You’re impossible.”<br>“You gonna kiss me or what?”<br>“If I don’t, you’re just going to kiss me anyways, aren’t you?”<br>Again, he gave me a grin. “You finally got that?”<br>“Impossible,” I muttered.<br>“Kiss me, Duchess.” </i><br><br>C’mon, doesn’t that make you smile?!<br><br>And I have to just say that Kristen Ashley writes the. BEST. epilogues. <i> EVER!!!! </i> The HEA was perfect and beautiful and I ended the book wiping my happy tears &lt;3<br><br>I don’t think I’ll be able to stop myself from going straight to book 2 of this series…<br><br>How I see Max and Nina:<br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380756297i/3120099._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aestas Book Blog</a><br><br>And come join the Aestas Book Blog <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook Page</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8401212965840211564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ℳelody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ℳelody" href="/user/show/4439079-elody">♥ℳelody</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1008717376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3539806731138483579"><b>DNF @ 45%</b> <br/><br/>I give up. <br/><a href='http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/angry/frustration%20alert/794237.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749142.gif' alt=' photo 794237.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><a href='http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/not%20impressed/does-not-get-it.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749143.gif' alt=' photo does-not-get-it.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>My first Kristen Ashley read and most likely my last. I've heard so much about her books, I finally got around to trying one and unfortunately the experience was not so great. Rather miserable to be honest. Just gonna get straight to the problems...<br/><br/><u>
  <b>THE WRITING</b>
</u><br/><a href='http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/not%20impressed/its-like-diah.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749144.gif' alt=' photo its-like-diah.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>Dear gawd. There is absolutely no structure or editing in this. It's a looooong-winded mess with no direction. I needed to re-read a Lisa Kleypas book to flush this out of my system. Gah.<br/><br/><b>-Use of parenthe</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3539806731138483579" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 45%</b> <br><br>I give up. <br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/angry/frustration%20alert/794237.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749142.gif" alt=" photo 794237.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/not%20impressed/does-not-get-it.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749143.gif" alt=" photo does-not-get-it.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>My first Kristen Ashley read and most likely my last. I've heard so much about her books, I finally got around to trying one and unfortunately the experience was not so great. Rather miserable to be honest. Just gonna get straight to the problems...<br><br><u>
  <b>THE WRITING</b>
</u><br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/not%20impressed/its-like-diah.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749144.gif" alt=" photo its-like-diah.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Dear gawd. There is absolutely no structure or editing in this. It's a looooong-winded mess with no direction. I needed to re-read a Lisa Kleypas book to flush this out of my system. Gah.<br><br><b>-Use of parenthesis</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Charlie, as ever (if he'd been there but, unfortunately, he was not), was right"</i>
</blockquote><br>What is the point of this?! Someone explain this to me because I really don’t understand this superfluous writing approach. It's totally unnecessary. Stating the obvious is one thing but doing it constantly and in such a manner is <i>super</i> annoying and very disruptive. It breaks up sentences that are already fragmented or ridiculously long so it's hard to follow along. The writing does not flow well because of this. <br><br><b>-Emphasis on wrong words.</b> KA has this strange tendency of italicizing words that do not need emphasizing and only manages to make the characters sound strangely juvenile.<br><blockquote>"He cracked two eggs <i>into</i> the side of the skillet <i>with</i> the bacon <i>and</i> the bacon grease and I stared." </blockquote><br>Just...WTH?<br><br><b>-Fragment and Run-on sentences.</b> They wreaked havoc throughout the book. The inner dialogue is riddled with endless rambling sentences that have no end and are hard to follow. Words are missing in some places, incomplete sentences that just hang there and make no sense in other places. <br><blockquote>
<i>"And, I also had to admit, no matter where I went and what I did, Niles didn't seem bothered with whether I arrived safe and sound. He didn't check in, even if I was traveling for work and would be away for a few days. And when I checked in, he didn't seem bothered with the fact that I was checking in. Or, lately (because I tested it a couple times), when I </i>didn't<i> check in and then arrived home safely, sometimes days later, he didn't seem bothered by the fact that I hadn't checked in." </i>
</blockquote><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/horrified/anigif_enhanced-27490-1403113286-1.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749145.gif" alt=" photo anigif_enhanced-27490-1403113286-1.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>-Summarizing and repetition of words. </b> <br><blockquote>
<i>"After doing that, I cleaned up my face. Then I threw another log on the fire. Then I stared at the log burning, trying to sort out my head. Then I failed at sorting out my head. Then when it got late, I made dinner for one and ate cookies for dessert. Then I read until it got later." </i> </blockquote><br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/angry/frustration%20alert/tumblr_lps76r3f341r00k3po1_400.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407640864ra/10749263.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_lps76r3f341r00k3po1_400.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>WHAT'S WITH ALL THE LISTS??! Stop stop stop it. <br><br><b>-Shitty grammar:</b> 'the further fact', contentish, nice-ish, fuckeva, a-fuckin-gain.<br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/angry/frustration%20alert/rhonj-dan-enough.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438040262ra/15659203.gif" alt=" photo rhonj-dan-enough.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>-Flat characters.</b> There is no substance or dimension to the characters in this story. All the men talk the same. And it doesn’t help that the entire story is being told in first person by the heroine, so readers are already at a disadvantage. But the bizarre dialogue and over the top reactions and mannerisms does not fit the characters KA tries to bring to life. A nineteen year old girl who was raped 3 weeks prior and is in an abusive relationship does not "skip-dance" everywhere she goes and "cry for joy" so easily. Like huh? Very cartoonish and inaccurate. <br><br>Which brings me to my next major bone to pick...<br><br><u>
  <b>MAIN CHARACTERS</b>
</u><br><b>Nina-</b> Our heroine is one inconsistent spineless stuttering mess with zero personality. She’s a 37 year old British-American lawyer who’s supposedly confident, independent and has had years of experience with men—- 8 relationships to be exact. Yes EIGHT. Bwaha! Yeah...ok. Yet she comes across as oblivious, stammering, huffy, frigid, defensive and unbelievably dense to certain things. It’s obscene how every little thing needs to be pointed out to this woman. Whenever she’s around Max, the "Hunky Colorado Mountain Man" she’s reduced to this:<a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/confused%20ditzy/243qbsw.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749146.gif" alt=" photo 243qbsw.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/confused%20ditzy/7_7.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749147.gif" alt=" photo 7_7.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/confused%20ditzy/tumblr_inline_mngeczhW0d1qz4rgp.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407699815ra/10755338.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_mngeczhW0d1qz4rgp.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/confused%20ditzy/i-dont-know-how-to-answer.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749148.gif" alt=" photo i-dont-know-how-to-answer.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/confused%20ditzy/tumblr_lnt60jT5JZ1qjt6d6o1_500.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749149.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_lnt60jT5JZ1qjt6d6o1_500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>She's a stammering mono-syllable confused idiot who parrots and repeats everyone else’s simple questions. The countless ‘I-...Um...Sorry?’ <b>DROVE ME FUCKING NUTS!</b> She’s confused when someone asks a question, when someone changes the subject, when someone tries to pay her a compliment. How is this woman a <i>lawyer</i>? For someone who's apparently so smart she seemed to be the last one to buy a clue or would point out the obvious to everyone like she's sherlock and solved a mystery. RME. Good grief. Am I seriously supposed to relate to someone like her? It just made no sense and was unreal. Make it a drinking game, take a shot every time this woman says <i>I’m sorry?</i> in this book and I promise you will be knocked off your butt after just 50 pages.<br><br>Here are some examples of our brilliant attorney:<br><br><i>She shook her head and announced, “Damon did this.”<br>“Did what?” I asked stupidly, feeling my heart start beating faster and my palms start itching.<br>“Your car, honey,” Max answered, and I looked at him. <br>“My car?” I repeated..<br>He tipped his head to the rental and his arm slid around my shoulder. “Damon, he did that to your car.” </i><br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/angry/frustration%20alert/tumblr_m8tgdbdmKQ1r3yaj6.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749150.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m8tgdbdmKQ1r3yaj6.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>***************<br><br><i>"Hello? Nina?"<br>My body jolted and I asked "What?" <br>He grinned and asked back, "Baby, you awake?"<br>"Um..."<br>"Sit down."<br>"But-"<br>"Sit down."<br>"All right." I muttered.</i><br><br>*************<br><br><i>“So, Nina, you come back with Max?" Harry asked me.<br>“Back?” I asked him.<br>“Yeah,” Harry said grinning a somewhat goofy grin.<br>“Um….” I replied, answering his confusing question the only way I could. “No”</i><br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/angry/frustration%20alert/tumblr_lw3u42TcMx1r3ovdbo1_400.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407639722ra/10749151.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_lw3u42TcMx1r3ovdbo1_400.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I just….can’t. <br><br><b>Max-</b> He’s the most cardboard-like hero I think I’ve read in a Contemporary setting. Nothing about him impressed me. He’s a walking cheesy overly-sentimental <i>extremely</i> macho stereotype. Like..where did you get this guy?<br><a href="http://s1177.photobucket.com/user/Melodious87/media/Gifs/Guys%20POV/tumblr_mfgswhNhzi1rii9pfo1_500.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438821705ra/15759462.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mfgswhNhzi1rii9pfo1_500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>He’s a rugged alpha man in his 40s but doesn’t talk like one at all. The endless slang, excessive swearing with words like ‘fuckeva’ and ‘a-fuckin-gain’ made it worse. Get serious. I found none of it attractive or realistic. And I had a hard time understanding what Max saw in Nina that had him so quickly enamored with her. He’s calling her cutesy names like ‘Duchess’ ‘baby’ and ‘babe’ just after 2 days of meeting her and taking liberties like they are in a full fledged relationship. Very odd. Apparently to him she’s the cutest thing in the world when she gets angry and he goes from not caring at all to being wildly attracted to her because she’s a big softy when she's passed out unconscious with the flu. 😒 Yeeeeah...nope. <br><br>There was absolutely zero build-up or momentum with these two. I only read up to page 259 and the only thing I got was them ‘making out’ constantly and Nina waffling and finding endless excuses to leave Max. Didn't even manage to get to the first love scene. This was a book that had no business being 688 pages long when all you have is endless droning on and chewing scenery. <i>
  <b>Nothing</b>
</i> happens.<br><br>Clearly this wasn’t a winner for me. I have a few other works by KA on my TR list but I’m not sure if I can sit through another round of this. She’s not for everyone that’s for sure. I have quite a few GR friends who’ve given her work high ratings but even so, the overall issue people have is with her writing--which I'm honestly surprised could ever be overlooked. Unfortunately for me the writing is the deal breaker and something I could not ignore. There was no way for me to even get into the story, what little there was of it, with all the ridiculous bizarre hiccups I kept encountering. <br><br>Sorry Kristen Ashley is not for me.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/256501710?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen">Kristen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-characters">fabulous-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=playboy-womanizer-manwhore">playboy-womanizer-manwhore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=scrumptious-hero">scrumptious-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=endearing-heroine">endearing-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=outstanding-epilogue">outstanding-epilogue</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer256501710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2096876621840950208"><b>Solid 4 stars</b><br/><br/>Wow! Kristen Ashley is one fantastic storyteller! I adore her charismatic characters, her intimate writing style, and her fabulous, sexy, overprotective, alpha heroes. Her heroes are truly swoonalicious!<br/><br/>Overall, I really enjoyed <i>The Gamble.</i> I did feel the book was a tad long-winded and wish the hero and heroine spent more time together without the constant interruptions from the secondary characters. With that said, I still loved this story. I loved Max's and Nina's characters. I lo</span>
  <span id="freeText2096876621840950208" style="display:none"><b>Solid 4 stars</b><br /><br />Wow! Kristen Ashley is one fantastic storyteller! I adore her charismatic characters, her intimate writing style, and her fabulous, sexy, overprotective, alpha heroes. Her heroes are truly swoonalicious!<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed <i>The Gamble.</i> I did feel the book was a tad long-winded and wish the hero and heroine spent more time together without the constant interruptions from the secondary characters. With that said, I still loved this story. I loved Max's and Nina's characters. I loved their chemistry, as well as their bantering. I did have a few small issues with their lack of communication (i.e., talking about Max's deceased wife) and Nina's inability to utter more words than Um... Max... and I'm sorry?  Those small annoyances, however, were not enough to hinder my overall enjoyment of the story. (Note: I might tear my hair out in frustration if all Kristen Ashley's heroines use the term "I'm sorry?" when not comprehending a question or statement. Just saying.).<br /><br />The secondary characters were superbly developed, entertaining, endearing, and, frankly, nuttier than fruitcakes! There were times I felt Nina and the cast of characters belonged on an episode of the <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_zsmzITXGu4&amp;feature=youtube_gdata_player" rel="nofollow noopener">Jerry Springer Show</a>.  It became <i>that</i> kind of crazy! That being said, I couldn't help but fall in love with them. <br /><br />The best part of <i>The Gamble</i>, other than Max, was the epilogue. It's become my favorite epilogue to date. It was poignant, heartwarming, and left me with happy tears and a full heart. Thank you Kristen Ashley for another great story with a lot of heart-and-soul. <br /><br /><i>If you're already a Kristen Ashley addict, or interested in checking out her books, be sure to stop by our <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/66492.Kristen_Ashley_Addict_s_Support_Group" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristen Ashley Addict's Support Group</a> here on Goodreads!</i></span>

<div id="review_416700256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416700256" />
    <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy"><img alt="Stacey is Sassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474185067p2/12062194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416700256?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey is Sassy" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy">Stacey is Sassy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/23278786-the-gamble">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=kristen-ashley">kristen-ashley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=best-of-the-bestest">best-of-the-bestest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=cont-series">cont-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416700256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6344095582973805985"><b>Kristen Ashley magic...or my blind devotion?</b><br/><br/>I absolutely love this story, but sometimes I feel guilty. It makes me feel like a hypocrite. It sort of has cheating in it, sort of has Nina trapped against her will and is completely OTT insta-love.<br/><br/>It must just be KA magic. I'm blinded to the things that would normally make my eye twitch. I honestly never saw those things when I initially read it and had to have someone tell me.<br/><br/>How the hell does she do it? Magic, I tell you...<br/><br/>**********<br/><br/><b>The Gamble def</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6344095582973805985" style="display:none"><b>Kristen Ashley magic...or my blind devotion?</b><br><br>I absolutely love this story, but sometimes I feel guilty. It makes me feel like a hypocrite. It sort of has cheating in it, sort of has Nina trapped against her will and is completely OTT insta-love.<br><br>It must just be KA magic. I'm blinded to the things that would normally make my eye twitch. I honestly never saw those things when I initially read it and had to have someone tell me.<br><br>How the hell does she do it? Magic, I tell you...<br><br>**********<br><br><b>The Gamble definitely paid off.</b><br><br>I've decided that my re-reads will be done on audio. With my busy schedule and real life, I don't have time to enjoy my re-reads anymore. The beauty of audiobooks is that you can listen to them anytime. I listen to them when I'm exercising, baking, doing school pick-ups (obviously not when my little munchkin is in the car) and when I'm mucking around on Pinterest. As these are re-reads, I don't need to worry that I'll miss something important or need clarification on a plot point, it's just a nice and relaxing way to keep reading while I'm doing stuff.<br><br><i>The Gamble</i> was one of the first books I read by Kristen Ashley and I have a signed paperback that sits on my shelf and never gets touched. If I want to see the message inside...I look at the photos I took. I want it to stay in mint condition. I wasn't sure how the audio would go, to be honest. Nina's character is an American who has spent a lot of time in England and has a "bit" of an accent. The narrator managed Nina's English accent perfectly while also giving Max a fantastic slow and smooth drawl. I always knew when the characters were changing as there was a slight difference in the accents and the way they talked which made it easy to distinguish them.<br><br>Max and Nina's story is still one of my favourites. Nina comes to America from England to have a break from her fiancé and to decide if she really wants to stay with him. They had been having difficulties in the relationship leaving Nina concerned she was making the wrong decision. Unfortunately, Niles, the fiancé, wasn't listening when Nina voiced her concerns and didn't really see any problems with the way things were. It doesn't take Nina long to realise that she doesn't really matter to Niles and his work was a lot more important to him than she was. Even when she finally explains this all to him, he can't be bothered or is too busy to "deal" with it. I was glad to see the back end of Niles.<br><br>Max has faced heartache and managed to keep going even though he's not happy. When Nina rocks up to his house for her holiday, they realise a mistake had happened and Nina's holiday destination will need relocation. Stuff happens, Nina's sick, the plans are a mess and Max ends up having to nurse Nina back to health. It doesn't take Max long to realise that Nina is awakening feelings in him that he hasn't had for a very long time. He knows he wants more with Nina and doesn't want to see her return to England. When Niles eventually comes out to see what the problem is, Max explains to Niles where he went wrong and why he doesn't get to keep Nina.<br><br><i>The Gamble</i> is at times funny and at times so sad you can't help but shed a tear. All of these emotions are hard to hold back as you're sitting in your car out the front of your kid's school. The squirming at the set of lights when Max is speaking all husky and smooth, demanding that Nina "tell him" (while he's deep inside her) the words he wants to hear. The crying when your heart is breaking for the woman who feels dirty and unclean. The laughing out loud when Nina turns into Zombie Nina in the mornings. But generally, this book just leaves me with a smile on my face.<br><br>I still love <i>The Gamble</i> and the audio just reinforces my love.<br><br><br>To buy <i>The Gamble</i> from Amazon - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/1QIuPmO">http://amzn.to/1QIuPmO</a><br><br>To buy the audio of <i>The Gamble</i> from Amazon - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/1SEnQ0U">http://amzn.to/1SEnQ0U</a><br><br><b>I’m an Aussie chick who loves to read and review romance, drink coffee, be a <i>Style Setter</i> and stalk David Gandy. To see more of my reviews, fashion, food and pervathons -</b><br><br><a href="http://staceyissassy.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447925695i/17069306.jpg" width="170" height="170" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/Sassyreviews" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004243.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="https://www.pinterest.com/Stacey1565/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004244.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="https://www.twitter.com/StaceyisSassy" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004245.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6344095582973805985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_381178983" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381178983" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381178983?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381178983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16126969459471457676">Loved this book... The main reason I loved it? <b>Max!</b><br/><br/>Nina is tired of her life. Living in England, engaged to a boring man who never listens to her, she decides she needs a time out. This brings her to the Colorado mountains for a two week get away. She arrives to the house she's rented, only to find there had been a mix up. The owner Max is in town. After getting in an argument, Nina decides to leave for a hotel. But its storming. And she is really ill. She ends up in a ditch and none other than </span>
  <span id="freeText16126969459471457676" style="display:none">Loved this book... The main reason I loved it? <b>Max!</b><br /><br />Nina is tired of her life. Living in England, engaged to a boring man who never listens to her, she decides she needs a time out. This brings her to the Colorado mountains for a two week get away. She arrives to the house she's rented, only to find there had been a mix up. The owner Max is in town. After getting in an argument, Nina decides to leave for a hotel. But its storming. And she is really ill. She ends up in a ditch and none other than Alpha Mountain Man Max &lt;3 nurses her back to health. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Duchess, remind me never to get you that riled. You're a handful when you're angry but you're hell on wheels when you're seriously pissed."</b>
</i><br /><br />Now there is a lot of drama going on in this little mountain town right now. Nina meets a lot of new people who she falls in love with right away. You will love these supporting characters! I know I did! Mindy, Brody, Jeff, Cotton, Arlene, Nina's mom and Steve- but no one could hold a candle to Max. What a man! He could be overprotective and a little possesive, but he was also incredibly sweet(Oh I <b>loved</b> the nicknames: Duchess, honey, baby, darlin'...) Couldn't get enough of Max!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"You're being domineering again."<br />"Yeah, baby, fair warnin', when we're naked, you better get used to that."</b>
</i> <br /><br />I actually really loved Nina as well. She was funny and cute, but she also didn't take any crap. She stood up for her self and other people. I loved her interaction with Mindy and some of the other characters. She had tragedy in her life with past relationships and her brother Charlie, but she used her past to help others which is an admirable thing to do. <br /><br />This was a really good read, loved the characters and the writing. The book was a little long, but it didn't feel that way. There was just a lot of story and it really gave you time to get to know the characters- it wasn't at all rushed. The ending was great, nothing better than an epilogue that leaves a huge smile on your face! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"There was a time in my life where I used to roll the dice. I did it a lot and I always lost. Every time, I lost and when I lost, I lost everything. So I got scared of rolling the dice. Thank you for showing me it was worth taking a gamble again, darling. It feels good to finally win and win huge."</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16126969459471457676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer271556593" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15475884800919768933"><br/>There are already many excellent reviews of this book, so I’m going to keep mine short - <br/><br/>I kept seeing Kristen Ashley’s name show up on my Goodreads friends’ status and review updates, so I had to see for myself what all the hoopla was about! Well, to be honest, I can't quite put my finger on it, but whatever it is about this book and this author, I’m sold! The writing isn’t flawless and it took me a bit to get used to the author’s style, but once I did it was easy to read and I couldn't put it </span>
  <span id="freeText15475884800919768933" style="display:none"><br />There are already many excellent reviews of this book, so I’m going to keep mine short - <br /><br />I kept seeing Kristen Ashley’s name show up on my Goodreads friends’ status and review updates, so I had to see for myself what all the hoopla was about! Well, to be honest, I can't quite put my finger on it, but whatever it is about this book and this author, I’m sold! The writing isn’t flawless and it took me a bit to get used to the author’s style, but once I did it was easy to read and I couldn't put it down. The characters are often times annoying as hell, especially Max who is, hands down, one of the most obnoxious, domineering men I’ve ever had the pleasure of reading about. The story itself is all over the place and yet easy to follow and a joy to read. <br /><br />The bottom line - Sometimes heartwarming, sometimes tragic, <i>The Gamble</i> is a funny, romantic, hot story, one I truly, <i>truly</i> enjoyed!<br /><br />-----<br />If you're a Kristen Ashley addict, or just interested in checking her books, be sure to stop by our <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/66492.Kristen_Ashley_Addict_s_Support_Group" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristen Ashley Addict's Support Group</a> here on Goodreads! <br /></span>

<div id="review_258092366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258092366" />
    <a title="Shawna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna"><img alt="Shawna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574172018p2/1802746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258092366?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawna" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna">Shawna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of small town contemporary romance &amp; sexy alpha heroes</span></div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2571524447758573150">5+ stars – Contemporary Romance<br/><br/><b>
  <i>The Gamble</i>
</b> is my second Kristen Ashley read, and I enjoyed it as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258093485' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sweet Dreams</a>, mainly because yummy, protective alpha hero Max actually rocked my world more than SD’s Tate. Nina and Max were great together, and the story kept me completely engaged, despite the fact that it’s very lengthy. <b>
  <i>The Gamble</i>
</b> is another winner, and I’m looking forward to reading more from this author. 5 stars!<br/><br/>One of my favorite scenes is when Max mops the floor with Nina’s sn</span>

She was a week away from me, she walked into a room I was in holdin’ another man’s hand, I’d lose my fuckin’ mind. Not at her. Wonderin’ where I lost my way and I’d talk to her about how to find my way back.”</i>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/808846184?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer808846184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3722440252612635361"><b>4 Stars<i> (Originally Read 1/2/2014)</i></b><br/><br/><b> 3.5 Stars<i> (Re-Read 2/8/2017)</i></b><br/><br/><b>4 Stars<i> (*2nd Re-Read 3/27/2019)</i></b><br/><br/><b>4 Stars<i> (**3rd Re-Read 8/10/2020)</i></b><br/><br/><b>**3rd Re-Read Note:</b> Not much to add here. I was in the mood for a KA re-read and I enjoyed it. It’s not my absolute favorites of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2958084.Kristen_Ashley' title='Kristen Ashley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kristen Ashley</a>, but it’s one I obviously enjoy returning to every once in a while. Good characters, good small town vibes, and good romance. Still frustrated with Max’s reactions but appreciated how he admits when he was wrong, and I would’ve </span>
  <span id="freeText3722440252612635361" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars<i> (Originally Read 1/2/2014)</i></b><br /><br /><b> 3.5 Stars<i> (Re-Read 2/8/2017)</i></b><br /><br /><b>4 Stars<i> (*2nd Re-Read 3/27/2019)</i></b><br /><br /><b>4 Stars<i> (**3rd Re-Read 8/10/2020)</i></b><br /><br /><b>**3rd Re-Read Note:</b> Not much to add here. I was in the mood for a KA re-read and I enjoyed it. It’s not my absolute favorites of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2958084.Kristen_Ashley" title="Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristen Ashley</a>, but it’s one I obviously enjoy returning to every once in a while. Good characters, good small town vibes, and good romance. Still frustrated with Max’s reactions but appreciated how he admits when he was wrong, and I would’ve loved more of an extended HEA, but that’s my greed showing. Overall it is a good, reliable book that I will probably continue to re-read 😊<br /><br /><b>*2nd Re-Read Note:</b> This was enjoyable as another re-read. I'm in a major book funk, so this helped a little in that I knew going in that I was going to enjoy it. I liked their relationship and I liked the kookie side characters that KA always does really well. I wasn't bothered too much with the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[dead spouse <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> touchy subject, but again I did have some issues with how Max handled Nina finding out. I also still wanted more with the epilogue. Otherwise, a good re-read and enjoyable enough that I'm going to up my rating to the original 4 stars (mainly because I'm happy I could rely on this for a solid read after feeling meh about so much). <br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b> I'm not feeling like I liked this as much as I did the first go-round, so I'm dropping my rating from 4 stars to 3.5. It might just be that I had read it before, so the mystery of what was going to happen wasn't there -- but who knows. I was a little disappointed in the H not being upfront with the h about his past, and I was really disappointed how he acted when he found out that she knew some of it. I have to say because of that whole thing I don't think of him as one of my favorite KA heroes. This does have a theme that I know many readers have issues with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the dead wife <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and while I normally don't get bothered by it -- this bugged me a little here. I understood all of the h's hesitations and inner thoughts regarding the H's past so it made me sympathize with her, and maybe that was why I wanted a better reaction from the H regarding the whole situation.<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Nina and Max's story. Nina is taking a "time-out" from her neglectful fiancé and leaves England to stay in a cabin in the Colorado mountains. She is shocked when she arrives and there is a grumpy mountain man telling her she has to leave. Max owns the house she rented, and there was a mistake made to where he is home. After a not-so-great introduction, they part ways only for Max to save Nina and nurse her back to health after a nasty flu. Nina then finds herself in an awkward situation where Max won't let her leave. She gets sucked into lots of town drama, some family drama, and the sexy Max...and they do eventually fall in love and get a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>POV:</b> This was told in Nina's POV (with a section of the epilogue in Max's POV).<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Ok. I found the end oddly abrupt where the rest is kind-of drawn out. I never skimmed, but was a little tempted to at times (maybe partially because I've read this before).<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> Kind of. They know each other a short period of time (a week!) before those stronger feelings are developed, but I still found it believable.<br /><br /><b>H rating:</b> 3 stars. Max. He was ok. I wish that he was more upfront with Nina.<br /><br /><b>h rating:</b> 4 stars. Nina. I liked her. She was kind of crazy, but I think that's part of why I did like her.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low, no tissues needed this time around -- I do remember shedding a few tears the first time I read it though.<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ They both push away at times. I would say that the H is the main pursuer of the relationship.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Good. They have some good chemistry and scenes, but not so much it takes away from the story.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>Safe sex:</b> Not really <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They do discuss birth control, but the h mentions in her inner dialogue that she didn't take them properly (but doesn't share that with the H). They don't use condoms, and I don't remember any mention of previous practices or std statuses.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>OW/OM drama:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There is both an ex of the H and an ex of the h that cause some drama for the h and H  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No <br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b>Not with mcs <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Mentions of side character being cheated on. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Kind of, but extremely short (hours). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There was no mention or suggestion of other partners during this time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rape (side character off page), suicide of loved one (h's brother off page), domestic violence (h with ex off page), loss of a spouse and miscarriages (H off page), violence/kidnapping/murder (on page), and suicide attempt by loved one (side character on page).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This had a little bit of an abrupt ending with a jump ahead epilogue and a HEA. I would've liked more time experiencing them working through some of their logistical issues, maybe Max's proposal, pregnancy, etc. We all know I'm greedy ;)<br /><br /><b>How I got it:</b> I bought it from Amazon for $3.71 back in 2014.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be either <u> Safe </u> Or <u>Safe with exception</u> for most readers depending on personal preferences.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have both the h and H pushing away<br />- <b> Does</b> have a very short separation (hours) between the h and H<br />- <b> Does </b> have abuse (not by mcs)<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have OTT sad parts<br />- <b>Does </b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
